The Council at its Meeting on the ioth October, resolved Address to the Mayor. unanimously :— ' I hat the best thanks of the Council be given to Councillor Alexander Glegg, J.P., for his able, courteous, and impartial conduct in the Chair, and for the time and attention bestowed by him in the discharge of his duties as Mayor of this Borough." 8. The General Purposes Committee were instructed to prepare an address expressing the Council's high appreciation of Councillor Glegg's services, and the following address was accordingly engrossed, framed, sealed with the common seal of the Council, and presented to Mr. Glegg at the Meeting of the Council on the 9th November, viz. :— Metropolitan Borough of Wandsworth. Population. Area. Rateable Value. 296,020 9,221 acres. ^ji>935»i6i. To Alexander (Jlisgg, Ksq., J.P. We, the Mayor, Aldermen, and Councillors of the Metropolitan Borough of Wandsworth, desire, upon your retirement from the Office of Mayor, to express our high appreciation of the valuable services which you have rendered to the Borough during the year of your Mayoralty, November, 1905—November, 1906. The Distress Committee established under the Unemployed Workmen Act, 1905, is much indebted to you, as its Chairman, for your constant attention, and for the sound judgment and knowledge of industrial matters which you brought to bear upon the difficult questions with which the Committee had to deal. Owing in a great measure to your exertions an Open-air Bathing l.ake has been constructed on Tooting Common in this 33 Borough, which found work for about 250 unemployed men, and has proved a most successful undertaking, in this connection we also reccrd with great pleasure the kindly sympathy shown by the Mayoress and yourself in providing a dinner and entertainment in the winter for a large number of the unemployed at Clapham. By your generous hospitality, and by the Public Receptions which vou have held of Inhabitants of the Borough specially interested in Sunday School work, in General Education, and in other Religious and Social subjects, you have shown a broad-minded conception of your Mayoral duties which has enhanced the respect felt for your high Office, and you have fully maintained in every way its usefulness and popularity. The many public Ceremonies which you have attended as Mayor include the Flower Show of the Southfields Children's Horticultural Society, at which the prizes were distributed by Her Royal Highness the Princes? Alexander of Teck, and the Dedication of the handsome Clock and Tower at Clapham Cross, which >ou presented, when the Lord Mayor and Lady Mayoress and the Sheriffs of the City of London were present in state to show their appreciation of your munificent and useful gift. The admirable manner in which you have discharged your Magisterial duties, your able, courteous, and impartial conduct in the Chair at the Council Meetings, and the great interest you have taken, not only in the business of the Council but in the affairs of the Borough generally, deserve our hearty recognition. We specially desire to express our cordial thanks to the Mayoress for the kindly and graceful manner in which upon so many occasions she has entertained her guests, and for the time which she has so ungrudgingly given in attending and supporting the numerous social and public functions in which you have been called upon to take part. It is our earnest hope that the Mayoress and yourself may long enjoy health and happiness, and that for many years to come the Borough will have ti»e benefit of your services as a Member of the Council. Sealed by Order. (Signed) James Wise, Mayor. Henry George Hills, Town Clerk. L.S. November cjth, 1906. 9. Councillor Anderson, on behalf of the subscribers bers of the Council) presented four silver fruit dishes to Mrs. Glegg as a mark of appreciation of her services in the discharge of the duties of Mayoress during the past year. Presentation to Mayoress. 10. Councillor Glegg presented to the Council a Chairman's ivory hammer with silver band and inscription. Chairman's Ivory Haiumer presented by Councillor Glegg 34 11. The Mayor (Councillor Glegg) presented to the Borough a tower and clock which he had erected on the public-way at Clapham Cross. The tower is about 25 feet high and the four dials of the clock are illuminated at night. The clock was unveiled by the Lord Mayor of London on the 19th July, 1906, and Alderman Bulcraig accepted charge of it on behalf of the Council. At the Meeting of the Council on the 1st August, the following resolution was passed by the Council, viz. :— Public Clock, Clapham Cross. "That the best thanks of the Council be presented to the Mayor for his gift of the public clock which he has erected at Clapham Cross, and that the Mayor and Mayoress be congratulated on the excellent arrangements made by them in connection with the ceremony." 12. Alderman John Gay resigned his office as Alderman in September, 1906. The resignation was accepted with regret, and the thanks of the Council presented to Alderman Gay for the very valuable services which he rendered to the Borough for so many years. In December, 1906, the Lord Mayor of London opened a fund for the PurPose °f raising the sum of £60,000 for the establishment of a specialised institution for the relief of the crippled children of London, and he asked for the assistance of the Mayors of the Metropolitan Boroughs in the matter. The Mayor (Councillor Wise) opened a branch fund for this Borough. The Town Clerk was appointed honorary secretary and treasurer, circulars were addressed to residents in the Borough inviting subscriptions to the Fund, and a concert was held at the Wandsworth Town Hall 011 the 25th February, and another at Streatham on the 31st May. The receipts to the 31st July w ere as follows, viz. :— Crippled Children. 37 £ s. d. Subscriptions 167 0 10 Proceeds of concert at Wandsworth 263 4 10 Proceeds of concert at Streatham 200 0 0 £630 5 8 Of this sum £601 15s. 4d. has been forwarded to the Lord Mayor, who in thanking the Mayor and all who had assisted in the movement in this Borough asked the Mayor to keep the Fund open until his term of office expires in November next. This the Mayor has decided to do. 26. The Council considered the subject of its representatives _ in the deed of covenant and consols set aside as security for the Borough Treasurer, and decided that Sir William Lancaster and Councillor Lidiard should continue to act as such representatives. Treasurer's Security. 27. In January last a letter was received from the Local Govern- ment Board forwarding copy letter and copy petition signed by 460 electors of the Tooting Ward calling attention to the inadequate representation of that Ward on the Council. Statistics dealing with the matter were prepared by the Borough Accountant, upon consideration of which the Council decided to inform the Local Government Board that, in the opinion of the Council 110 prima facie case was at present made out for a re-apportionment of the members of the Council. A further letter was received from the Local Government Board in May stating that the Board had decided to cause a Local Inquiry to be held into the matter, and enclosing copy of a letter which the Board had received from the Streatham Ratepayers Association, and stating that the Inquiry would extend to the proposals contained in such letter for the division of the Borough into ten wards. No date has yet been fixed for the proposed Inquiry, and the subject is at present under the consideration of the General Purposes Committee. Representation of Wards. 28. Alderman Hewett and Councillor Ball were appointed the Council's representatives to attend a Conference convened by the Paddington Borough Council on the subject of the desirability of placing a legal limit upon the precepts levied by Boards of Guardians and Central Spending Authorities of London. Conference re Precepts. 38 The Conference decided to ask for the opinions of the Metropolitan City and Borough Councils as to the desirability of placing a limit upon the expenditure of Precepting Bodies, the desirability of reform in the administration of the Poor Law, and of a greater proportion of the expenditure upon education being borne by the Imperial Exchequer, and upon other matters. Councillor Ball having ceased to be a member of the Council, Councillor Comins was appointed one of the Council's representatives in his place. Other meetings of the Conference were held, and in May, 1907, the following resolutions were passed, viz. :— (1) That in the opinion of this Conference the administration of the Poor Law should be in the hands of the Borough Councils, who are called upon to levy the rates for this purpose. (2) That in the opinion of the Conference each Borough Council should elect a representative on the County Council, thus furnishing the additional membership repeatedly asked for in view of the additional duties imposed on the County Council. (3) That the foregoing resolutions be submitted by the delegates to their respective Councils, in order that the opinions of the Councils upon the subjects may be obtained and considered at a subsequent meeting of the Conference and decision arrived at as to whether any, and if so what action should be taken for obtaining legislation to carry out the views indicated. This Council decided to take no action in the matter at present. 29. The Council considered a resolution passed by the Wimbledon Wimbledon Corporation urging the Conservators of Wimbledon Common. Common to provide facilities for the public to obtain tea and other light refreshments on Wimbledon Common. The Council concurred in such resolution, and appointed the Mayor and Councillor Mathias as its representatives on a deputation to the Conservators in favour of the suggestion. The deputation attended on the 28th May, 1906, when the Conservators resolved that until further order the wives of the common keepers and labourers should be permitted to supply hot water to visitors to the common, and that the question of other refreshments should be further considered. Wimbledon Common. 30. In April, 1906, this Council asked the London County Council t0 provide sanitary conveniences on Wandsworth Common. In reply the Parks Committee of the London County Council stated that they did not see their way to recommend Wandsworth Common. 39 the County Council to construct or to contribute towards the cost of constructing such conveniences, but that they were prepared to recommend the granting of a site for above ground conveniences, if this Council at its own expense, or jointly with the Battersea Borough Council, would agree to erect and thereafter maintain them. This Council informed the County Council that as that Council was the authority having the control of the Common, and responsible for its upkeep, the Council was of opinion that it was the duty of the County Council to provide sanitary conveniences on the Common, as had been done on other open spaces under its control. 31. This Council, with other Metropolitan Boroughs, sealed a memorial to the Local Government Board urging the necessity of an amendment of the law relating to combined drainage. The Local Government Board stated that they were not at present in a position to promise to introduce legislation on the subject. The attention of the Prime Minister, the President of the Local Government Board, and the Parliamentary representatives of the Borough has been again called to the necessity of legislation on the subject. Combined Drainage. 32. The Council considered twelve notices of intention to apply for new licenses for the sale of intoxicating liquors, and decided to oppose two applications for full licenses in respect of premises at the corner of Replingham Road and Wimbledon Park Road. The applications were refused. Licenses. 33. Notice of objection to the renewal of certain licenses on account of the condition of sanitary conveniences was also given. The necessary works having been carried out the notices were withdrawn. 34. At the request of the Justices the Medical Officer of Health and Sanitary Inspectors were authorised to give evidence at the Licensing Sessions as to the sanitary condition of certain premises and the requirements of the neighbourhood. 35. Application having been made for a music and dancing license in respect of " Waratah," King's Road, Clapham Park, the Council opposed the application on the grounds that the required c 4° notice to the Council had not been given, and that the premises in question were unsuitable for the purpose. The application was refused. 36. The accommodation for the staff of the Public Health PePartment at Huguenot Place not being sufficient, the department has been transferred to No. 90, East Hill, Wandsworth. Public Health Department. 37. In August last the Council considered the subject of the abatements made to owners of property of an annual value of not exceeding £20. The practice adopted at that time was to rate the owners instead of the occupiers of such premises, and to allow them the statutory abatement of 15 per cent., with a further abatement of 10 per cent, where the owners were willing to pay the rates whether the premises are occupied or not. The Council decided that from the 1st April, 1907, the last mentioned abatement of 10 per cent, should be reduced to 5. Bating of Small Property. 38. Councillors Campbell, Cresswell, and Gridley attended as the Council's representatives a conference of representatives of Local Authorities and Labour Organisations held in October last to consider the action of the District Railway Company in increasing the fares charged to passengers. Resolutions were passed by the Conference protesting against the action of the Company in increasing the fares, and urging the necessity of joint action with the view of obtaining a reduction of fares on the District Railway, and that the County Council should be asked to make application to the Board of Trade to institute an inquiry under the Cheap Trains Act into the question of increased fares, insufficient trains and accommodation on such railway. As the ordinary and workmen's fares from the stations on the Company's lines in this Borough had not been increased this Council took no further action in the matter. Eailway Pares. 39. The testing of the electricity supplied in the Borough by the County of London Electric Supply Company, which has been the subject of long correspondence between this Council and the County Council, has been again considered, and the County Council were urged to take steps without further delay to secure the due testing of the supply, ai d to compel the Company to provide t(.'sting stations in accordance with the provisions of their Electric Lighting. 41 Order. In reply the County Council stated that the Company had intimated their willingness to establish, as a beginning, seven testing stations in their areas of supply. Four of these are to be provided in this Borough—one at the Council House. 40. The following Parliamentary Bills were considered by the Council, viz.:— a. ' Parliamentary Bills. Parliamentary Elections (Hours of Poll). 42 Plural Voting Sale of Whisky* Telegraph (Construction) Vagrant Children* Vaccination Vaccination Prosecutions. 41. This Bill proposed to authorise the County Council to laydown and maintain new tramways in various parts of Lonaon. I .on don County Council (Tramways and Improvements). 42. The only new tramway in this Borough was No. 14, to commence in Queen's Road by a junction with the existing tramway, passing along a short length of new road, proposed to be constructed under the provisions of the Bill, between Queen's Road and Heath Road, thence along Heath Road and Silverthorne Road, and joining the existing tramway in Wandsworth Road. This proposal was made in order to avoid the widening of Wandsworth Road, which would be necessary if the single line there was converted into a double line. 43. The Bill also proposed to authorise the reconstruction of tramways at Vauxhall, Loughborough, Norwood and Camberwell, and the following lines (partly within this Borough), viz.Wandsworth and Vauxhall line—From East Hill to a point in Wandsworth Road, opposite the Eastern end of Nine Elms Lane; atid the Queen's Road line—From Lavender Hill to a point in Queen's Road, near the junction of Robertson Street. 44. Clause 17 would have authorised the County Council to form the new street above-mentioned, so as to connect Queen's Road with Heath Road, and to effect the following widenings in this Borough :— Wandsworth Road— (a) On the Northern side between Silverthorne Road and a point half a chain or thereabouts Eastward thereof. (b) On the North-Western side between Salvin Street and New Road. (c) On the South-Eastern side— (i.) Between the Easttrn side of the railway bridge over Wandsworth Road and a point half a chain or thereabouts North-Eastward thereof. (ii.) between Albion Road and a point opposite the North-Eastern side of Pensbury-street. 43 45- Clause 23 provided for a contribution by each of the Boroughs where widenings were to be carried out, of one»:hird of the nett cost thereof. 46. Clause 37 proposed to amend Section 12 of the London County Tramways (Electrical Power) Act, 1900, relating to thedrainage of tramway rails and the removal therefrom of the accumulations of matter by providing that such accumulations should be deposited by the County Council in any receptacle for street refuse provided by the Road Authority in the street, and be removed by the Road Authority as other street refuse. 47. This Council objected to the proposal to construct a loop line along Queen's Road, Heath Road and Silverthorne Road, being of opinion that the portion of Wandsworth Road between Silverthorne Road and Queen's Road should be widened, and a double line of tramways constructed there, and also suggested the widening of Wandsworth Road near Union Grove and Nursery Street, and a small widening at East Hill, and that this Council's contribution towards the cost of improvements should be limited to a specified sum. This Council also objected to the proposed amendment of Section 12 of the Electrical Power Act, 1900. That section, which provided that the County Council shall remove all matter removed from the conduit or grooves of tramway rails, was inserted at the instance of the late Wandsworth Board of Works, and has worked satisfactorily. 48. The County Council did not agree to this Council's suggestion as to the construction and re-construction of the tramways in this Borough, and as this Council adhered to its objections the provisions relating thereto were withdrawn from the Bill. 49. The clause relating to the removal of matter taken from the conduits and grooves of tramways was withdrawn and a new clause inserted empowering the County Council and Road Authorities to enter into agreements for such removal. 50. The Bill as amended, was passed and received Royal Assent on the 21 st August, 1907. 51. This Bill would authorise the Medical Officer of the County Council to take samples of milk produced, sold or intended for sale within the county, to enter dairies London County Council (General Powers). 44 within or without the county, and inspect the cows kept therein, and would,empower the County Council, upon a report that tuberculosis is likely to be caused to persons from the consumption of milk from the dairy, to order the dairyman not to supply milk within the county. 52. The Bill would also authorise the Medical Officer of the London County Council to inspect dairies in the case of infectious disease suspected to be attributable to the consumption of milk therefrom, to take samples of milk at any place (including railway stations) within the county, would require dairymen to supply lists of farms from which their supply of milk is derived, and lists of their customers, and to notify the County Council of all cases of infectious disease among their employees, and would prohibit infected persons from milking animals. Sanitary authorities were also to be empowered, with a view to prevent the spread of infectious disease, to require laundrymen to furnish a list of their customers. 53. Clauses 38 and 39 dealt with the subject of the provision of a proper supply of water, and accommodation for the cooking and storage of food in houses let in separate tenements. Clause 40 would prohibit the sorting of house refuse by hand, Clause 41 proposed to make certain sanitary regulations for premises used for the sale, &c., of food for human consumption, Clause 42 would have authorised the County Council to make bye-laws to regulate the conduct of the businesses of a vendor of fried fish, fish curer, and marine store dealer; and Clauses 49—51 proposed to empower Metropolitan Borough Councils to establish, maintain and carry 011 milk depots for the sale of milk for consumption by infants under two years of age. 54. Part VII. related to the cleansing of verminous persons, and would authorise the examination of school children and the inmates of any common lodging-house, and require Sanitary Authorities to secure the cleansing of verminous persons. 55. The Bill also proposed to authorise the County Council to cater at their lodging-houses. 56. The Council presented a petition against certain provisions of the Bill, and the following points were included in the petition, viz.:— 45 (a) Clauses 21-31 (relating to milk) to be amended so as to relate only to milk suspected to be tuberculous, and Borough Council Officers to have the powers sought in their respective districts. (b) That Clause 32 (infectious disease attributable to milk) be objected to on the ground that the proposed remedy should be provided by amending Clause 71 of the Public Health (London) Act, 1891. and that the County Council should only act upon information of a Medical Officer of Health of a Sanitary Authority. (c) That Clause 33 (taking samples of milk at railway stations) be opposed on the ground that this duty should remain as at present in the hands of the Sanitary Authority. (d) Clauses 34 and 35 (lists of customers to be supplied by dairymen in certain cases, and infectious diseases among dairy servants) that these powers, if granted, should be conferred on borough Councils wno already have powers within the county. (e) That clause 36 (infected persons not to milk animals) be objected to, the matter being provided for in London by Section 69 of the Public Heath Act. (f) That Clause 37 (lists of customers of laundries in certain cases) be amended so as to include list of persons employed. (g) That Clauses 39 and 40 (accommodation for keeping and storage of food in tenement houses and prohibition of sorting house refuse by hand) be opposed as unnecessary. (h) That Clauses 49-51 (power to Borough Councils to establish milk depots) be objected to. (i) That Clause 84 (power to County Council to cater at lodging-houses) be opposed as being unnecessary. With the exception of Clauses 21—31 relating to milk supply, the clauses to which this Counpil objected, and the clauses relating to water supply, sale of food, t>ye-laws as to fried fish shops, &c., catering by County Council, were afterwards withdrawn, and the part of the Act relating to the cleansing of verminous persons amended so as to enable the County Council and Sanitary Authorities to enter into arrangements with respect to such cleansing. 57. The Bill, as amended, received the Royal Assent on the 28th August, 1907. 58. This was a Bill to confer powers on the London County Council with respect to the supply of electrical energv in bulk in the Administrative County of London and London County Council (Electric Supply). 46 certain neighbouring areas in the Counties of Essex, Kent, Surrey and Middlesex. 59. The Bill also provided that the County Council might apply for a Provisional Order to enable them to supply energy to any district within the area of supply in which no supply was afforded, and would authorise the Council and any Companies authorised to supply energy to agree for the supply by or to the Council of energy in bulk or otherwise. 60. The Bill would also authorise the County Council to acquire the local undertaking of any of the scheduled distributors except the undertakings vested in the Borough Councils of St. Marylebone and Woolwich. 61. The Council petitioned against the Bill on the grounds that whilst admitting that legislation was required, as the development of electricity in London was backward, it was not desirable that the County Council should become an authority to supply electricity in bulk or otherwise; that the scheme was ill-considered ; that the proposed area of supply was too large ; that the proposal to purchase the undertakings of the local authorities would involve a large expenditure of public money without adequate return, the generating works of some of the local authorities being probably of less commercial value than the outstanding debts and liabilities; that in the hands of the County Council the undertaking would result in a loss, which under the provisions of the Bill was to be made good out of the County Rate ; and that the undertaking should be established and carried on as a commercial undertaking, the County Council to be the controlling or supervising authority as in the Electric Lighting Acts. 62. The Bill was read a second time in the House of Commons and referred to a Committee, with an instruction that if any power was conferred upon the London County Council to transfer or lease to any company, local authority, body or person any of the powers, duties or liabilities entrusted to it by the Bill, the conditions upon which such power should be exercised should be embodied in the Bill or in a subsequent Bill. After a lengthy enquiry the Committee reported against the Bill. 47 63. This was a Government Bill to enable the Board of Trade by Provisional Order to authorise the compulsory acquisition of land for generating stations by any local authority, company, or person within or without their area of supply or district; the supply of electricity in bulk ; and the supply to railways and tramways partly within and partly without the area; and to authorise the Board, in the case of a Provisional Order for the supply of electricity in bulk only, or in bulk and for power only, to exclude from the Order the provisions as to purchase contained in Section 2 of the Electric Lighting Act, 1888, in respect of the undertaking for the supply in bulk. The Bill was withdrawn before reaching second reading. 64. This was a Bill to provide for uniform scales of charges for water throughout the limits of the Board's supply, the charge for water for domestic purposes not to exceed 5 per cent. of the rateable value. " Domestic purposes" was defined as including water-closets and baths constructed so as not to contain more than 50 gallons, but not including a supply of water for any of the following purposes:—Steam engines, railway purposes, warming or ventilating purposes, working any machine or apparatus, consumption by or washing of horses or cattle, washing carriages or other vehicles, watering gardens, fountains, or other ornamental purposes, cleansing sewers and drains, cleansing and watering streets or roads, fire extinction, flushing drains by means of any apparatus discharging automatically, public pumps, baths, or washhouses, any trade manufacture, or business, and any bath constructed so as to contain more than 50 gallons. 65. The Bill would authorise the Board to supply water by measure, and provided that they should not be bound to supply otherwise than by measure for trade or manufacturing purposes, or to common lodging houses, barracks, &c., and that the charge by measure should not exceed is. per 1000 gallons. The charge for water for public purposes was fixed at 6d. per 1000 gallons. 66. The Council presented a petition against the Bill with the view of obtaining the following amendments :— (a) That, except as hereinafter mentioned, the basis of charges for supply for domestic purposes be rateable value. Supply of Electricity. Metropolitan Water Board (Charges, &c.). 48 (b) That domestic purposes include water for gardens not exceeding an area of one-eighth of an acre, and that gardens exceeding one-eighth of an acre be supplied with water by meter. (c) That there be one uniform rate for all rateable values up to £150 and a lower rate in respect of all rateable values exceeding £150, the higher rate to be charged on the first £150 of any rateable value. (d) That the Water Board should have power to make special arrangements with regard to large properties using very little water. (e) That in exceptional cases the Water Board should supply water by meter if required by consumers. (f) That the charge for supplying and maintaining meters be 7½ per cent. of the cost of the meter; and that the London County Council be the authority for testing meters. (g) That the limit of size of baths exempted from additional charge be extended from 50 gallons as proposed to 80 gallons. 67. The Bill was considered by a joint Parliamentary Committee and, as amended by them, provided that in the case of premises occupied for the purposes of trade or business assessed at more than £300 per annum, the Board may make a rebate of not less than 20 nor more than 30 per cent. ; and that the charge for a supply by meter should be from 7d. to is. per 1,000 gallons. The Bill also fixed the charges for the hire, etc., of meters, and provided that domestic supplies were to include baths of a capacity of 80 gallons and to exclude watering gardens by means of any outside tap or any hose, tube, pipe, sprinkler or other like apparatus. The Bill received the Royal Assent on the 28th August, 1907. 68. This Bill proposed to authorise the Water Board to carry out certain works, amongst which were the construction of conduits or lines of pipes in the southern part of the Streatham Ward, and a new road between Leonard Road and Greyhound Lane, and for the purpose of one of the conduits to make connections and attachments to the bridge carrying Greyhound Lane over the London Brighton & South Coast Railway. The Bill also proposed to authorise the Board to take part of Streatham Common, amounting to 1 acre 2 roods 18 poles, and to construct and maintain telegraphs for communication with works, to require aseparate supply pipe to be laid from the main pipe into each M etropolitan Water Board (Various Powers). 49 separate tenement, and would prevent persons supplied with water other than by measure from fixing tubes or hose to the pipes for the purpose of washing horses or carriages or for watering gardens, washing pavements, etc. The Bill would also authorise the Board to supply, repair, or alter pipes, water closets, apparatus and receptacles permitted by their regulations, and to repair injury to or defect in communication pipes and to recover the cost from the person requiring the same. 69. The Council presented a petition against the Bill, dealing with the following matters :— (а) Depth and position in which conduits or pipes will be laid ; provisions for the protection of the roads and sewers of the Council; for providing that the proposed new road in this Borough shall be formed, sewered, paved and lighted to the satisfaction of this Council; that no posts or wires or aqueducts, etc., be placed upon or over any highway in the Borough. (b) The words "watering gardens or" to be deleted from Clause 61,. which would prevent the fixing of tubes or hose to service pipes. (c) That the charge for the supply and maintenance of meters be per cent. of the cost of the meter ; and that the London County Council be the authority for testing meters. (d) Water Board to be liable for damage to highway caused by the bursting of mains or pipes. . (e) Clause 68 (power to supply cisterns, baths, water closets, appar atus, etc.) to be amended so that the Board shall comply with the requirements of the Public Health (London) Act and Bve-laws. 70. The Council was also represented at a Conference of City and Metropolitan Borough Councils with reference to this and the Charges Bill, and upon considering the resolutions passed at the Conference was of opinion that the power to supply materials should not be conferred upon the Water Board, and that the provisions requiring separate tenements in the same house to be supplied by separate pipes were objectionable and unnecessary. 71. The clause relating to the formation of a new road at Streatham having been withdrawn, the question of garden watering and meter rents, dealt with by the Charges, etc., Bill, and the Council being satisfied with the arrangements made by the 50 Water Board as to the depth and position of mains, the Council did not further oppose the Bill, which received the Royal Assent on the 28th August, 1907. 72. This Bill proposed to give the Company powers with respect to the purchase and use of lands at Mitcham, the consolidation and conversion of stock, and the raising of additional capital. The Bill proposed to repeal the section of the Company's Act of 1867, limiting the price of gas to 5s. 6d. per 1,000 cubic feet, and to fix the standard price at 3s. 9d., subject to the usual sliding scale (to which the Company were not subject). The Bill also contained provisions relating to the illuminating power, the apparatus to be used for testing, and as to penalties for defect in illuminating power, etc. The Company also sought powers to lay pipes in streets not dedicated to public use, to sell, let for hire, or otherwise deal in, but not manufacture, engines, stoves, ranges, etc., to supply in bulk beyond the limits of supply, and to lay mains, pipes and culverts for procuring, conducting, or disposing of oil or other materials used or resulting from the manufacture of gas or any residual products. 73. The Council petitioned against the Bill upon the following matters, viz. :— (a) The financial provisions of the Bill. (ft) That Clause 15 be amended so as to provide that notice as to the sale of stock shall be given to this Council as well as the Councils of other districts in the Company's area of supply. (c) That the proposed standard price of 3s gd. per thousand cubic feet is too high (the present price charged by the Company being 3s. 6d.) and that the proposed reduction of the illuminating power from 15 to 14 candles should carry a reduction in the price of gas. (d) That Clause 30 be opposed with the view of substituting a flat flame burner for the argand burner for testing illuminating power ; that the proposed table photometer be excluded on account of its unreliability, and that local authorities have power to appeal to the Board of Trade to prescribe any other photometer or standard light as well as the Company. (e) That the provisions that the Company shall not be liable to any penalty in respect of any defect in illuminating power unless the average of three consecutive tests made at intervals of not less than one hour be less than the prescribed illuminating power be objected to, and that a penalty be incurred in respect of one test as at present. Mitcham & Wimbledon District Gas. 51 (/) That provisions be inserted for testing calorific power, and for tests to be made at any time, or with greater elasticity as to times, than as prescribed by the Gas Works Clauses Act, 1871. (g) That a proviso be added to Clause 34 similar to that in the Wandsworth and Putney Gas Act, 1900, that before laying or relaying pipes in streets not adopted by local authorities, notice be given to the local authority, who shall notify the reasonable depth and position where such pipes are to be laid. (h) That Clause 40 be amended so that pipes for ancillary purposes may only be laid in this Borough with this Council's consent. (3s. gd. proposed by the Bill). (b) Additional capital £240,000 (,£300,000 proposed by the Bill). Borrowing powers £80,000 (£100,000 proposed in the Bill). Also power to borrow a further sum of £15,000 in respect of the old capilal. The Bill received the Royal Assent on the 4th July, 1907. 76. This Bill provided that the consent of the owner, lessee, and occupier of a dwelling-house to the use for burials of any ground used or appropriated for a cemetery, mentioned in Section 9 of the Burial Act, 1855, shall not be and shall be deemed never to have been required in any case where the dwelling-house is or was begun to be erected after any part of that ground has or had been so used or appropriated; and was promoted to meet the case of burial authorities whose cemeteries would be affected by the decision in "Godden v. Hythe Burial Board," to the effect that the above-mentioned consents must be obtained, even if the house is erected after the ground had been used or appropriated for a cemetery. This decision would have seriously affected the use of cemeteries, and a Conference of Burial Authorities was held at Lambeth, at which this Council was represented, and a resolution was passed calling attention to the unsatisfactory state of the law in the matter and to the necessity of the immediate amendment of Section 9 of the Burial Act, 1855. A deputation was appointed to wait upon the Government, and the President of the Local Government Board introduced the above Bill, which received the Royal Assent on the 21 st December, 1906. Burial Act, 1906. 53 Local Authorities (Transfer of TreasuryPowers). 77. This Bill provided that the Local Government Board should exercise, as regards every local authority in England, except the London County Council, any powers conferred on the Treasury by any enactment contained in, applied by, or incorporated with the Baths and Washhouses Acts, or the Burial Acts, or any local or private Act, as respects dealings with property, loans, and matters connected therewith. The Council took no action with regard to the Bill, which received the Royal Assent on the 4th August. South Eastern & London, Chatham & Dover Railway. 78. So far as related to this Borough, this Bill proposed to extend, for a period of two years from the 6th August, 1907, the time for the compulsory purchase of lands and the execution of works in connection with railway widenings near Wandsworth Road Station, authorised by the Company's Act of 1900. No action was taken by the Council thereon, and the Bill became law on the 4th July, 1907. Butter and Margarine 79. This was a Bill to make further provision with respect to the manufacture, importation, and sale of butter and margarine and similar substances. On the Bill coming before a Committee of the House of Commons a new clause was inserted extending the powers contained in the Margarine Act, 1887, so as to enable Inspectors of Weights and Measures to take samples of margarine. The Council deemed it inexpedient that such powers should be conferred on Inspectors of Weights and Measures, and petitioned the House of Lords to strike out the clause. Justices of the Peace (No. 2). 80. This Bill dealt with the qualification of County Justices, and provided that a solicitor might be appointed a County Justice, and that any person who was a Justice of the Peace by virtue only of his office might be excluded from the exercise of his functions by the same authority by which other Justices can be removed from the Commission of the Peace. The Council made no order on the Bill, which passed and received Royal Assent on the 4th August. Advertisements Regulation. 81. This was a Bill to authorise Local Authorities (in London the County Council and the City Corporation) to make bye-laws with respect to advertising hoardings and the exhibition of advertisements. The Council 54 sented a petition in favour, and suggested to the County Council that a provision should be inserted in the Bill to the effect that the bye-laws before being made should be submitted for the consideration of the Metropolitan Borough Councils, by whom they are to be carried out. The County Council stated in reply that the Home Office authorities were not prepared to accept an amendment to give effect to the suggestion. The Bill was passed. Education (England & Wales). 82. This Bill, introduced by the Government, provided that schools should not be recognised as public elementary schools unless provided by the local education authority, and contained provisions for the continuance of existing voluntary schools as provided schools, and with respect to religious instruction, the transfer of teachers and their duties, and other matters. It also dealt with the making of schemes with respect to educational endowments and the powers of the Board of Education as to the administration thereof, and proposed to authorise the establishment of a central education authority for Wales. In the opinion of the Council the Bill would have laid a heavy burden upon the rates and taxes of the country without effecting any corresponding improvement in the means of education, and, in view of the Education Acts of 1902 and 1903, unnecessary. A petition was, therefore, presented against the Bill, which passed the House of Commons, and, after considerable amendment, was read a third time in the House of Lords. It was, however, eventually withdrawn. Education (Administrative Provisions). 83. This Bill would, amongst other things, give the Local Education Authority the same powers with regard to the purchase of land for the purposes of higher education as they now possess for the purposes of elementary education, and powers with respect to the appropriation and alienation of land and buildings. The Council being of opinion that, with regard to higher education, the Metropolitan Borough Councils should be consulted before the site of a school is determined upon, and should also appoint Managers of higher elementary and secondary schools, as is now done in the case of elementary schools under Section 2 of the Education (London) Act, 1903, presented a petition for the alteration of the Bill to this effect. The amendments asked for were, however, not madeand the Bill received the Royal Assent on the 28th August, 1907. 55 Education (Bpecial Religious Instruction). 84. This was a Bill providing for the payment to the Local Education Authority by the Managers of non-provided schools in which religious instruction is given which would not be permissible in a school provided by the authority under Section 14 of the Elementary Education Act, 1870, of a sum equal to one-fifteenth part of the sum paid in salaries to the teachers who have been employed in the school and have given that instruction. The Council petitioned against the Bill on the grounds that the Local Education Authority does not pay rent for the school buildings, and, assuming that one-fifteenth to fourteen-fifteenths is the true proportion of denominational to secular education in non-provided schools, then the Local Education Authority should in justice pay to the Managers fourteen-fifteenths of the rental value of the buildings as rent; and that the Bill should not be passed unless a provision to that effect was inserted. The Bill was withdrawn. Elections (Meetings in Schoolrooms). 85. The object of this Bill was to entitle any Member of Parliament, or of County, District, or Parish Councils, or Boards of Guardians, and any candidate for election to such bodies, for the purpose of holding a public meeting in furtherance of their candidature, to the use of a suitable room in any public elementary school upon payment of a fixed charge. The Council petitioned for an alteration of the Bill so as to include Metropolitan Borough Councils in its provisions, but the Bill, after passing the House of Lords, did not reach second reading in the Commons. Factory & Workshop Act (1901) Amendment. 86. The object of this Bill was to distribute the working hours in laundries more regularly over the week, to substitute for the present variable periods of employment a fixed hour in the morning and another at night before and after which respectively work was not to be carried on, and to bring within the scope of the Factory Act, religious and charitable institution laundries, and the smaller laundries where long hours and insanitary conditions are frequently found. A petition was presented by the Council in favour of the Bill, which was afterwards dropped. Home Work Regulation. 87. This was a Bill to provide for the better regulation of home industries and required that all dwellingplaces in which work is done shall be certified by D 56 H.M. Inspector of Factories. The Council petitioned against the Bill, which was dropped before reaching second reading. Public Health Officers. 88. This Bill related to the qualification and tenure of office of Medical Officers of Health in Urban Sanitary Districts, and provided that Inspectors of Nuisances outside London should be called Sanitary Inspectors, and that Sanitary Inspectors, including those in London, should be appointed or removed only with the consent of the Local Government Board. The Council was of opinion that Sanitary Inspectors should be under the control of the Council by whom they were employed, and presented a petition against the Bill. The Bill was dropped before second reading. Public Health (Regulations as to Food). 89. This was a Government Bill to enable regulations to be made for the prevention of danger arising to public health from the importation, preparation, storage, and distribution of articles of food and drink intended for human consumption. The Council petitioned against the Bill on the ground that definite details should be given as to the extent and nature of the suggested regulations. The Bill received the Royal Assent on the 28th August, 1907. Sutton District Water- go. The London Brighton & South Coast Railway Company having proposed to sink a well near the Carshalton springs of the River Wandle, with the intention of conveying the water thus obtained along their railway for the general purposes of the railway, the above Bill was promoted by the Sutton District Water Company last Session, with the object of preventing water being obtained within the water company's area of supply for sale or use beyond that area without the express authority of Parliament being first specifically obtained, the water company being of opinion that the proposed well would affect the quantity of water available for their purposes and would also considerably reduce the quantity of water in the River Wandle. The Council presented petitions to both Houses in favour of the Bill, which received Royal Assent on the 4th August, 1906. Street Betting- 91. As mentioned in the last report (p. 39), two Bills were introduced (one in each House) providing that any person frequenting any street or public place for the purpose of betting shall be liable for a first offence to a 57 penalty of not exceeding £10, for a second offence £20, and for a third or subsequent offence, or where the person committing the offence has any betting transaction with a person under sixteen years of age, to a fine of £50 or to imprisonment for not exceeding six months. The Council presented petitions in favour of the Bills. The House of Commons' Bill was dropped, but the other Bill passed and received Royal Assent on the 21st December. 92. No action was taken with regard to the other Bills abovementioned. Patriotio School. 93. The London County Council in April, 1906, gave notice of their intention to accept the transfer from the Patriotic Fund Corporation of the school at the Royal Victoria Patriotic Asylum, Wandsworth Common, under the provisions of the Elementary Education Act, 1870. This Council objected to the proposal on the grounds that the school was a non-local one providing for the education of children from all parts of the country, that there did not appear to be any need, financially, for the transfer, and that the Corporation ought not to be relieved of their responsibility to maintain the school; and also asked the Board of Education to be allowed to be heard against the proposal. The Board of Education replied that they had considered this CounciPs representations, but, in view of the facts that the children in the asylum were resident in London, that the Patriotic Fund Corporation did not propose themselves to continue the school if the transfer did not take effect, and in that event it would be necessary for the County Council to find school accommodation for the children, involving the erection of a new school, they were not prepared to refuse to consider the proposal on the grounds of this Council's objection. The transfer was sanctioned and took effect on the 1st January, 1907. For the purposes of management the school has been added to the Garratt Lane, Swaffield Road, and Wandsworth Guardians Schools Group. 94. The Council has also had before it the subject of the expiration of the lease of the land belonging to the Patriotic Fund Corporation adjoining the asylum, and the London County Council were asked whether they had taken any steps with the view of the acquisition of the land to add to Wandsworth Common ; but the County Council replied that they did not see their 58 way to take any steps in the direction indicated. The County Council was then informed that this Council trusted that the County Council would see that the land in question was not built upon. Powers, duties and experience of Managers. 95.
